Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor of odontogenic origin that arises from the odontogenic epithelium in the jaw. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of odontogenic cyst that is associated with the crown of an unerupted tooth. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a break in one or more of the bones surrounding the eye. It can cause double vision, but it does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition in which the temporomandibular joint (TMJ) is fused, making it difficult or impossible to open the mouth. It can cause obstructive sleep apnea due to the inability to breathe properly through the mouth.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that occurs when blood flow to the heart is blocked, and it can lead to heart damage or death.
  Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the amount of cholesterol and triglycerides in the blood.
  HDL is known as "good" cholesterol, and high levels of HDL can help protect against heart disease.
  LDL is known as "bad" cholesterol, and high levels of LDL can increase the risk of heart disease.
  TG is triglycerides, which are a type of fat found in the blood.
  Rosuvastatin and atorvastatin are medications that belong to a class of drugs called statins, which are used to lower cholesterol levels.
  Fenofibrate is a medication that belongs to a class of drugs called fibrates, which are used to lower triglyceride levels.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  Based on the patient's lipid profile, the patient has high triglycerides and low HDL, which are both risk factors for heart disease. The preferred treatment for this patient would be a combination of a statin and a fibrate. Rosuvastatin and fenofibrate are both effective medications for this purpose. Therefore, the best option is A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Myocardial infarction is a condition where there is a blockage in the blood flow to the heart muscle. 
  Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the levels of different types of cholesterol and fats in the blood.
  HDL is the "good" cholesterol, LDL is the "bad" cholesterol, and TG is triglycerides.
  Statins are medications that are used to lower LDL cholesterol levels. 
  Fenofibrate is a medication that is used to lower triglyceride levels.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  The patient has high triglycerides and low HDL levels, which are both risk factors for cardiovascular disease. 
  Rosuvastatin is a statin that can lower LDL cholesterol levels, and fenofibrate is a medication that can lower triglyceride levels and increase HDL levels. 
  Therefore, the preferred treatment for this patient would be a combination of Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate.
Response 2:

  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that occurs when blood flow to a part of the heart is blocked, usually by a blood clot.

  Statins are a class of drugs that lower cholesterol levels in the blood.
  Fenofibrate is a fibrate drug that lowers triglyceride levels in the blood.

Response 4:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency in which the blood supply to a part of the heart is blocked, usually by a blood clot, leading to damage or death of the heart muscle.
  Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the amount of cholesterol and fats called triglycerides in the blood.
  HDL (high-density lipoprotein) is known as "good" cholesterol because it helps remove LDL (low-density lipoprotein) or "bad" cholesterol from the arteries.
  LDL (low-density lipoprotein) is known as "bad" cholesterol because it can build up in the walls of arteries, leading to atherosclerosis.
  TG (triglycerides) are a type of fat found in the blood that can contribute to the buildup of plaque in the arteries.
  Statins are a class of drugs that lower cholesterol levels in the blood by blocking the enzyme responsible for producing cholesterol in the liver.
  Fenofibrate is a drug that lowers triglyceride levels and raises HDL cholesterol levels.
  
Analysis:
  The patient had a myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, and the lipid profile reveals low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels. This indicates that the patient has dyslipidemia, a condition characterized by abnormal levels of lipids in the blood, which is a risk factor for cardiovascular disease. The preferred treatment for this patient would be a statin drug to lower LDL levels and reduce the risk of future cardiovascular events. Fenofibrate can also be added to the treatment to lower TG levels and raise HDL levels. However, the combination of rosuvastatin and fenofibrate is associated with an increased risk of adverse effects, such as myopathy and rhabdomyolysis, and should be used with caution. Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose and is not recommended as the initial treatment for dyslipidemia.

Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a cavity within the brain that is filled with cerebrospinal fluid (CSF).
  A: The optic stalk is a structure that connects the developing eye to the brain and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve, also known as the oculomotor nerve, is a cranial nerve that originates in the midbrain and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a stalk-like structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures that are part of the hypothalamus and are located posterior to the infundibulum, but not on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("D")

  C: The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus.
  D: The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain.

  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance

  T4 is a thyroid hormone that is important for growth and development.
  TSH is a hormone that stimulates the thyroid gland to produce T4.
  A: Primary hypothyroidism is a condition where the thyroid gland does not produce enough thyroid hormone, but it does not involve the pituitary gland.
  B: A pituitary tumor can cause abnormal hormone levels and growth problems, but it does not specifically involve the thyroid gland.
  C: A TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a type of pituitary tumor that produces excess TSH, which can cause the thyroid gland to produce too much T4. This can lead to growth problems and other symptoms.
  D: TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder where the thyroid gland is unable to respond to TSH, which can cause growth problems and other symptoms.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique used in periodontal surgery to gain access to the root surface of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface of the tooth has been exposed for 6 years.
  A: The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the cementum to the alveolar bone, but if the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is unlikely that the PDL fibres will still be attached to the cementum.
  B: The PDL fibres attach the cementum to the alveolar bone, but if the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is unlikely that the PDL fibres will still be attached to the dentin.
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is a common finding in cases where the root surface has been denuded for a long time.
  D: Co-adaptation to the remaining fibres is a common finding in cases where the root surface has been denuded for a long time.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root surface of a tooth.
  PDL fibres (periodontal ligament fibers) attach the tooth to the surrounding bone and cementum.
  Cementum is a layer of hard, mineralized tissue that covers the root surface of a tooth.
  Dentin is a hard, mineralized tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth structure.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the body or a body cavity.
  
Answer: "C" 
Explanation: 
  A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface. This is because the epithelial cells migrate and cover the previously denuded root surface in response to the loss of PDL fibers. The PDL fibers may not reattach to the cementum, and the remaining fibers may not co-adapt to the remaining fibers.

  B: If the PDL fibres are attached to the dentin, it indicates that the tooth is not healthy.

  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons

  C: HDL (High-Density Lipoprotein) is a type of lipoprotein that carries cholesterol from the tissues back to the liver. It has a density of 1.063-1.210 g/mL.
  D: Chylomicrons are lipoprotein particles that transport dietary lipids from the intestines to other locations in the body. They have a density of 0.95 g/mL.

  D: Chylomicrons are lipoprotein particles that transport dietary lipids from the intestine to other parts of the body. They have a density of 0.95 g/mL.

  C: HDL (High Density Lipoprotein) is a type of lipoprotein that carries cholesterol from peripheral tissues back to the liver.
  D: Chylomicrons are lipoprotein particles that transport dietary lipids from the intestine to other parts of the body.

  Type 2: Two separate canals leaving the pulp chamber and joining short of the apex to form one canal.
  Type 3: One canal leaving the pulp chamber, dividing into two, and rejoining short of the apex to form one canal.
  Type 4: Two separate canals leaving the pulp chamber and extending to the apex.
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is not a single, straight canal, nor two separate canals joining short of the apex, nor two separate canals extending to the apex. Therefore, it is not classified as Type 1, Type 2, or Type 4.

Topic: Pediatrics
Question: A neonate presents with jaundice and clay coloured stools. Liver biopsy shows giant cells diagnosis is –
Choices:
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - Jaundice is a yellowish discoloration of the skin and whites of the eyes due to high levels of bilirubin in the blood.
  - Clay-colored stools are pale, white, or light-colored stools that may be caused by a lack of bile in the stool.
  - A liver biopsy is a medical procedure that involves taking a small sample of liver tissue for examination under a microscope.
  - Giant cells are large cells with multiple nuclei that can be seen in various liver diseases.
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice can cause jaundice in newborns, but it is unlikely to cause clay-colored stools or giant cells on liver biopsy.
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia can cause jaundice, clay-colored stools, and giant cells on liver biopsy. This is a serious condition that requires prompt treatment.
  C: Physiological jaundice is a common condition in newborns that usually resolves on its own without treatment. It is unlikely to cause clay-colored stools or giant cells on liver biopsy.
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia is not a recognized medical condition.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Neonatal hepatitis is an inflammation of the liver that occurs in early infancy, typically within the first month of life.
  Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a rare disease of the liver and bile ducts that occurs in infants. It causes bile to build up in the liver, leading to jaundice, liver damage, and cirrhosis.
  Physiological jaundice is a common condition in newborns, characterized by yellowing of the skin and whites of the eyes due to high levels of bilirubin in the blood.
  Clay-colored stools are a sign of obstructive jaundice, which can be caused by extrahepatic biliary atresia.
  Giant cells are a type of cell that can be seen in liver biopsy samples from patients with viral hepatitis or autoimmune hepatitis.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - Jaundice is a yellowish discoloration of the skin and mucous membranes due to the accumulation of bilirubin in the blood.
  - Clay-colored stools are pale, white, or light-colored stools that may be caused by a lack of bile in the stool.
  - Neonatal hepatitis is a liver inflammation that occurs in the first month of life.
  - Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a rare disease of the liver and bile ducts that occurs in infants. It is characterized by the absence or closure of the bile ducts outside the liver.
  - Physiological jaundice is a common condition that occurs in newborns due to the breakdown of red blood cells and the immature liver's inability to process bilirubin effectively.
  - Giant cells are large cells with multiple nuclei that can be found in liver biopsies.
  
Analysis:
  - The neonate presents with jaundice and clay-colored stools, which are not normal in a neonate.
  - The liver biopsy shows giant cells, which indicates liver inflammation.
  - Option A and C mention physiological jaundice, but the presentation is not consistent with physiological jaundice.
  - Option D mentions physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia, but the liver biopsy shows liver inflammation, which is not consistent with physiological jaundice.
  - Option B mentions neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia, which is a possible diagnosis in this case.

Action: Answer("B")
